  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2853415271" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853415271" />
    <a title="Corie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69102738-corie"><img alt="Corie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533357798p2/69102738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853415271?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corie" href="/user/show/69102738-corie">Corie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345409324" href="/book/show/481559.Blood_and_Gold">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2853415271&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853415271" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6879174091135637065">I think Anne Rice is slowly starting to become one of my favorite authors. She has a way with words that is simply beautiful to me and I love the way she incorporates history into her works. The element of history is like another character altogether and it makes perfect sense because this series constantly grapples with what it means to die, to live in a timeless world where everyone you once loved as a mortal is gone, and those you have made immortal so that they may love you grow to resent yo</span>
  <span id="freeText6879174091135637065" style="display:none">I think Anne Rice is slowly starting to become one of my favorite authors. She has a way with words that is simply beautiful to me and I love the way she incorporates history into her works. The element of history is like another character altogether and it makes perfect sense because this series constantly grapples with what it means to die, to live in a timeless world where everyone you once loved as a mortal is gone, and those you have made immortal so that they may love you grow to resent you, battle you, run for you, but somehow always find there way back because love is as complex as the very preternatural beings that wield it as a weapon. It is not nearly as pretty or constant as many like to think. Often it can be rather uncomfortable, confusing, and blurring the lines between the replete and the predatory. Rice always does a good job of portraying this fact. This latest installment is closer to Interview With The Vampire and The Vampire Lestat in theme and style. That's probably why I enjoyed it so much.<br /><br />Instead of Revolutionary France or Antebellum Lousiana, our setting begins in Ancient Rome. The reader meets back up with Marius de Romanus a Patrician vampire created during the time Caesar as he tells his life story to a Viking vampire by the name of Throne. He tells Throne about his love for a woman vampire named Pandora, who he had loved when they were both humans. He brought Pandora into 'The Dark Gift' had hoped to mold into everything he wanted her to be and at one point 'broke her dreams with his forceful logic'. <br /><br />But Pandora is one who thinks for herself and speaks frankly and only wishes that he acknowledge that this is okay. That she should be allowed to love him and be her own person. This cumulates into a monumental disagreement wherein Marius rashly abandons her. He regrets it the moment he does it, but it is too late. So his travelings, actions, and witnessing of history for the next millennia represent mere distractions to keep him from confronting the pain of this decision. <br /><br />He tells the already touch upon stories of Mael and the Druids, Egypt and 'Those Who Must Be kept' and introduces new details about his time in Rome, Byzantine, Florence in the time of Botticelli, Venice, the Kievan Rus, England, and Saxony. At each destination, he attempts to create 'perfect time', while coming upon other ancient vampires, younger fledglings, and humans whom he would either love or despise. All of them, no matter what they represent, are poor substitutes for the one he really wants, Pandora. She inspires complex feelings in him. He loves and despises her in unison and he later realizes these feelings are an extension of the apprehension and burden he feels towards the parents of all vampires, Askaha and her consort Enkil. He would battle with ancient ones like Euxodia, abandon friends Mael and Avicus, and give humans the dark gift to deal with this torment. Marius cannot reconcile conflicting beliefs and actions. <br /><br />Upon finding Pandora again, Marius learns that you can have all the time in the world but it will never be enough to recover the love you have lost. The love is a different thing, it is transformed and altered. I especially enjoyed this part of the novel because it became clear Marius and Pandora are like the prototypes of all other major relationships in the Vampire Chronicles. It was eye-opening to see how much like Lestat, Marius truly is and explains his need to be Lestat's mentor. Because Marius could not find Pandora he created Armand and tried to mold him. And when Armand is taken by Santino, Marius takes Bianca so that she might love him. It is as Lestat created Louis for the loss of Nicolas and Gabrielle's love. And then later, when Lestat gives Claudia to Louis so that Louis might mold her. And how Euxodia tried to destroy Avicus in order to possess Marius is like how Armand did away with Claudia to have Louis all to himself. Both Euxodia and Armand fail in some way as the objects of their desires are devoted and have strong bonds to their companions.<br /><br />The vampire immortality brings wisdom is so many things but like humans, they lose reason and logic in regards to love. None of them are infallible but they cannot seem to conceive a new way of going about things. The most ancient ones Askaha and Enkil are a testament to this stubborn nature. Enkil in his vegetative state knows only to destroy those who threaten his position with Askaha.<br /><br /> It is the dance that keeps repeating time and again through the centuries, with the players expecting different outcomes though they stubbornly choose to do the same steps. It is insanity, but one they accept as 'vampire nature'. They must always learn, try getting the handle for things like the blind leading the more blind. They know the limitations of vampirism; that the ones who they want to know the most, they can't know because the minds of the creator and fledging are barred from one another.<br /><br />It seems then that Marius' story is an attempt at breaking the cycle. To arm Throne with as much logic and emotion because he wants Throne to understand the first hand the consequences of history repeating itself, of having confusing feelings, and letting anger determine one's path. Throne is tormented by the love he has for Maharet, but Marius' story cautions that he must not be rash, possessive or violent as he had done with Pandora. The only way those with immortality can survive the abandonment and loneliness from their kind is to accept that it inevitably comes with antiquity and to 'remember these complex creatures with love'. They only mean to handle this curse as best they can, be gentle and try to have patience. <br /><br />On a final note, I also enjoyed seeing the Talasamca in earlier centuries and liked the 'David Talbot like' character of Raymond Gallant. I hope later stories will clear up the origins of these scholarly mortals. It was fun seeing another similarity which Marius shares with Lestat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6879174091135637065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iTdEjiyqUTXZuhV2UdZrTSB3WSbLhp0sd90S65uB+FizES1cl/SYXX6RoRemI2GS9ii+7gULE0sso1RaVsIKwg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gr4Z/1az4Yo8cDWv5b3YD1lojzFfD2TW0DpMDyBhiZq4mHAt7e0o4ptbgc4SSNLQjzdo+ZGC6rGLRAq+7SJ7AA==')})
  }

I want everybody to cry when Claudia dies, just like they did for Little Nell.&quot;-- Anne RiceFebruary 8, 1995Interview with the Vampire. The Vampire Lestat. The Queen of the Damned. The Talc of the Body Thief Memnoch the Devil. With her bestselling, epic saga, Anne Rice has reinvented the legend and literature of one of fiction\'s most popular and captivating archetypes. Now, Katherine Ramsland, Anne Rice\'s biographer, has completely revised and updated the ultimate reference guide to the world, history, and adventures of these haunting characters, from the unforgettable Lestat to Rice\'s newest chilling creation, Memnoch the Devil.Written with the full cooperation of Anne Rice -- and now with more than 1,200 entries -- The Vampire Companion offers an insightful exploration, appreciation, and interpretation of all the characters and events, names and places, symbols and themes in the five volumes of The Vampire Chronicles, including more than one hundred pages of new entries on Rice\'s latest vampire novel, Memnoch the Devil. Everything that readers might want to explore further is annotated and analyzed in this entertaining and enlightening work: the unforgettable characters of Louis, Lestat, Claudia, Akasha, Armand, and Memnoch; the important points of interest on Lestat\'s fascinating tour through Heaven and Hell; ancient lore; Rice\'s unique contributions to the mythos of vampires; the literary inspirations that echo through the novels; Rice\'s own reflections and revelations about her work and about the movie Interview with the Vampire; and much more.Richly illustrated with new photos, drawings, maps, and a complete time line of events in The Chronicles, The Vampire Companion is as captivating as the phenomenal saga it explores. It is a guidebook that no visitor to the world of Anne Rice should be without.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8329373082689515805\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p3/7577.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">Anne Rice
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
21,711
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer299207449841307652">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText299207449841307652" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="299207449841307652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Louis recounts how he became a vampire at the hands of the radiant and sinister Lestat and how he became indoctrinated, unwillingly, into the vampire way of life. His story ebbs and flows through the streets of New Orleans, defining crucial moments such as his discovery of the exquisite lost young child Claudia, wanting not to hurt but to comfort her with the last breaths of humanity he has inside. Yet, he makes Claudia a vampire, trapping her womanly passion, will, and intelligence inside the body of a small child. Louis and Claudia form a seemingly unbreakable alliance and even &quot;settle down&quot; for a while in the opulent French Quarter. Louis remembers Claudia\'s struggle to understand herself and the hatred they both have for Lestat that sends them halfway across the world to seek others of their kind. Louis and Claudia are desperate to find somewhere they belong, to find others who understand, and someone who knows what and why they are.\n\nLouis and Claudia travel Europe, eventually coming to Paris and the ragingly successful Theatre des Vampires--a theatre of vampires pretending to be mortals pretending to be vampires. Here they meet the magnetic and ethereal Armand, who brings them into a whole society of vampires. But Louis and Claudia find that finding others like themselves provides no easy answers and in fact presents dangers they scarcely imagined.\n\nOriginally begun as a short story, the book took off as Anne wrote it, spinning the tragic and triumphant life experiences of a soul. As well as the struggles of its characters, Interview captures the political and social changes of two continents. The novel also introduces Lestat, Anne\'s most enduring character, a heady mixture of attraction and revulsion. in a feat of mesmeric storytelling, a chillingly hypnotic entertainment in which the oldest and most powerful forces of the night are unleashed on an unsuspecting world.Three brilliantly colored narrative threads intertwine as the story unfolds:- The rock star known as Vampire Lestat, worshipped by millions of spellbound fans, prepares for a concert in San Francisco.  Among the audience--pilgrims in a blind swoon of adoration--are hundreds of vampires, creatures who see Lestat as a &quot;greedy fiend risking the secret prosperity of all his kind just to be loved and seen by mortals,&quot; fiends themselves who hate Lestat\'s power and who are determined to destroy him . . . - The sleep of certain men and women--vampires and mortals scattered around the world--is haunted by a vivid, mysterious dream: of twins with fiery red hair and piercing green eyes who suffer an unspeakable tragedy.  It is a dream that slowly, tauntingly reveals its meaning to the dreamers as they make their way toward each other--some to be destroyed on the journey, some to face an even more terrifying fate at journey\'s end . . . - Akasha--Queen of the Damned, mother of all vampires, rises after a 6,000 year sleep and puts into motion a heinous plan to &quot;save&quot; mankind from itself and make &quot;all myths of the world real&quot; by elevating herself and her chosen son/lover to the level of the gods: &quot;I am the fulfillment and I shall from this moment be the cause&quot; . . . These narrative threads wind sinuously across a vast, richly detailed tapestry of the violent, sensual world of vampirism, taking us back 6,000 years to its beginnings.  As the stories of the &quot;first brood&quot; of blood drinkers are revealed, we are swept across the ages, from Egypt to South America to the Himalayas to all the shrouded corners of the globe where vampires have left their mark. Vampires are created--mortals succumbing to the sensation of &quot;being enptied, of being devoured, of being nothing.&quot; Vampires are destroyed.  Dark rituals are performed--the rituals of ancient creatures prowling the modern world.  And, finally, we are brought to a moment in the twentieth century when, in an astonishing climax, the fate of the living dead--and perhaps of the living, all the living--will be decided.From the Hardcover edition.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16573334430515543496\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n Both demon and angel, he is drawn to kill but tempted by goodness as he moves among the pantheon of Anne Rice\'s unforgettable characters. Julien Mayfair, his tormentor; Rowan, witch and neurosurgeon, who attracts spirits to herself, casts spells on others and finds herself dangerously drawn to Lestat; Patsy, country and western singer, who was killed by Quinn Blackwood and dumped in a swamp; Ash Templeton, a 5,000 year old Taltos whose genes live on in the Mayfairs. Now, Lestat fights to save Patsy\'s ghost from the dark realms of the Earthbound, to uncover the mystery of the Taltos and to decide the fate of Rowan Mayfair. Both of Anne Rice\'s irresistible realms - the worlds of Blackwood Farm and the Mayfair Witches - collide as Lestat struggles between his lust for blood and the quest for life, between gratification and redemption.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11309936142544919394\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer
